Griffith

A hymn of prayer and praise to Prithivi or deified Earth

Translation
  1. Great (bс╣Ыh├бnt) truth, formidable right, consecration, penance,
    br├бhman, sacrifice sustain the earth; let her for us, mistress of what
    is and what is to beтАФlet the earth make for us wide room (lok├б);тАФ
Notes

Found also in MS. (iv. 14. 11), which reads yajn─Б╠Бs in b, and
bh├║vanasya (for bh├бvyasya) in c. The Anukr. does not heed that
p─Бda a is jagat─л. The verse (unless more of the hymn is meant to
be included with it) is, according to V─Бit. 12. 6, to be repeated by one
who relieves on the ground the needs of nature. It is quoted by K─Бu┼Ы.
24. 24 in the ─Бgrah─Бyaс╣З─л ceremony; also in the comm. to 24.35 (cf.
above); and it, with vs. 38, is reckoned (see note to K─Бu┼Ы. 19. 1) among
the puс╣гс╣нika mantras.

Griffith

Truth, high and potent Law, the Consecrating Rite, Fervour, Brahma, and Sacrifice uphold the Earth. May she, the Queen of all that is and is to be, may Prithivi make ample space and room for us.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Unoppressedness in the midst of men (m─Бnav├б). Whose are the ascents
    (udv├бt), the advances (prav├бt), the much plain (sam├б); who bears
    the herbs of various virtue (n─Б╠Бn─Бv─лrya)тАФlet the earth be spread out
    for us, be prosperous for us.
Notes

The mss, vary in a between badhyat├бs and madhyat├бs (Bp.P.M.I.
have ba-), but only the latter can be right, and the translation
adopts it; the former (which Ppp. also has, and m─Бnaveс╣гu) seems to
have come in under the influence of -b─Бdham. тМКCorrect the edition.тМЛ As
the text stands, p─Бda a can only be an adjunct to vs. 1, and so Ppp.
reckons it, and begins our b with asy─Бs. But MS. (iv. 14. 11)
reads asamb─Бdh─Б╠Б y─Б╠Б madhyat├│ m─Бnav├йbhyo; it also has mah├бt for bah├║
at end of b, and n─Б╠Бn─Бr┼лp─Бs and bibh├бrti in c. This time the
Anukr. notices that b has 12 syllables. K─Бu┼Ы. 137. 16 quotes the
verse тМКin the preparation of the vediтМЛ.

Griffith

Not over awded by the crowd of Manu’s sons, she who hath many heights and floods and level plains; She who bears plants endowed with many varied powers, may Prithivi for us spread wide and favour us.

Translation
  1. On whom [are] the ocean and the river (s├нndhu), the waters; on
    whom food, plowings, came into being; on whom quickens this that
    breathes, that stirsтАФlet that earth (bh┼л╠Бmi) set us in first drinking.
Notes

That is, doubtless, give us precedence over others (but MS. reads
p┼лrvap├йyam: see note to vs. 5). Ppp. reads for b yasy─Бс╣Б dev─Б
тАЩmс╣Ыtam anvavindan; and for second half-verse it has our 4 c, d,
giving our 3 c, d as second half of vs. 5, with the easier reading
j─лvati, тМКfollowed byтМЛ vi┼Ыvam ej─Бt in c. We should expect

Griffith

In whom the sea, and Sindhu, and the waters, in whom our food and corn-lands had their being, In whom this all that breathes and moves is active, this Earth. assign us foremost rank and station!

Whitney
Translation
  1. Whose, the earth’s, [are] the four quarters; on whom food,
    plowings, came into being; who bears manifoldly what breathes, what
    stirsтАФlet that earth (bh┼л╠Бmi) set us among kine, also in
    inexhaustibleness (? ├бnya).
Notes

Ppp. reads in a yasy─Бm and pс╣Ыthivy─Бm, and in b gс╣Ыс╣гс╣нayas
тМКcf. note to ii. 13. 3тМЛ. As second half-verse it has our 5 c, d,
giving our 4 c, d as 3 c, d, reading (after bahudh─Б) pr─Бс╣Зine
jan╠Дgano bh┼лmir goс╣гv a┼Ыveс╣гu pinve kс╣Ыс╣Зotu, thus relieving us of the
difficult ├бnye. K─Бu┼Ы. (137. 17) uses the verse next after vs. 2, in
connection with making the sacrificial hearth four-cornered. The
description given by the Anukr. of this and the two following verses is
so wholly wrong that we cannot help suspecting a corrupt text. This
verse is, if we make no resolutions in d, a regular triс╣гс╣нubh.

Griffith

She who is Lady of the earth’s four regions, in whom our food and corn-lands had their being, Nurse in each place of breathing, moving creatures, this Earth. vouchsafe us kine with milk that fails not!

Whitney
Translation
  1. On whom the people of eld (p┼лrvajan├б) formerly spread themselves (?
    vi-kс╣Ы); on whom the gods overcame the Asuras; the station (? viс╣гс╣нh─Б╠Б)
    of kine, of horses, of birds (v├бyas)тАФlet the earth assign us fortune
    (bh├бga), splendor.
Notes

Ppp. reads in a nicakrire, and in b atyavartayan; also in
c (found as тМКitsтМЛ 4 c) vayasayya тМК?тМЛ. MS. has a verse made up
of our 5 a, b (without variant), 4 c (accenting bibh├бrti), and
3 d (with p┼лrvap├йyam). The verse is mixed triс╣гс╣нubh and jagat─л.
тМКIn Ppp. this verse precedes our 4.тАФThe sequence of the half-verses of
the Vulgate as they stand in Ppp. seems therefore to be as follows: 3
a, b, 4 c, d, 5 a, b, 3 c, d, 4 a, b, 5 c, d.тМЛ

Griffith

On whom the men of old before us battled, on whom the Gods attacked the hostile demons, The varied home of bird, and kine and horses, this Prithivi vouchsafe us luck and splendour!

Griffith

Firm standing-place, all-bearing, store of treasures, gold-breasted, harbourer of all that moveth. May Earth who bears Agni Vaisvanara, Consort of mighty Indra, give us great possessions

Whitney
Translation
  1. She the earth (bh┼л╠Бmi pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Б), whom the gods, sleepless, defend all
    the time without failureтАФlet her yield (duh) to us honey, what is
    dear; then let her sprinkle us with splendor.
Notes

The verse is found also in MS. (iv. 14. 11), which reads in c
ghс╣Ыt├бm instead of priy├бm.

Griffith

May Earth, may Prithivi, always protected with ceaseless care by Gods who never slumber, May she pour out for us delicious nectar, may she bedew us with a flood of splendour.

режрео рдпрд╛рд░реНрдгрд╡реЗрд╜рдзрд┐ рд╕рд▓рд┐рд▓рдордЧреНрд░ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. She who in the beginning was sea (salil├б) upon the ocean
    (arс╣Зav├б); whom the skilful (man─лс╣г├нn) moved after with their devices
    (m─Бy─Б╠Б); the earth whose immortal heart covered with truth is in the
    highest firmament (vy├▓man)тАФlet that earth (bh┼л╠Бmi) assign to us
    brilliancy, strength, in highest royalty.
Notes

The verse is properly 11 + 12: 11 + 11; 8 + 8 = 61 syllables, and not
very well described by the Anukr. The last two clauses perhaps have
independent construction: ‘[assign] to us brilliancy [and] strength,
[and] set [us] in highest royalty.’

Griffith

She who at first was water in the ocean, whom with their wond- rous powers the sages followed, May she whose heart is in the highest heaven, compassed about wit h truth, and everlasting, May she, this Earth, bestow upon us lustre, and grant us power in loftiest dominion.

  1. On whom the circulating waters flow the same, night and day, without
    failureтАФlet that earth (bh┼л╠Бmi), of many streams (-dh─Б╠Бr─Б) yield

Griffith

On whom the running universal waters flow day and night with never-ceasing motion, May she with many streams pour milk to feed us, may she bedew us with a flood of splendour.

Griffith

She whom the Asvins measured out, o’er whom the foot of Vishnu strode, Whom Indra, Lord of Power and Might, freed from all foemen for himself, May Earth pour out her milk for us, a mother unto me her son.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let thy hills (gir├н) [and] snowy mountains (p├бrvata), let thy
    forest-land (├бraс╣Зya), O earth, be pleasant (syon├б); upon the brown,
    black, red, all-formed, fixed (dhruv├б) earth (bh┼л╠Бmi), the earth
    guarded by IndraтАФI, unharassed, unsmitten, unwounded, have stood upon
    the earth.
Notes

Ppp. reads in b ─Бraс╣Зyaс╣Б corrected to ar-, and naс╕е after
astu; also in c lohin─лс╣Б, and in f adhi с╣гс╣нh─Бс╣Б, which is
better. тМКRoth’s Collation has in fact addhi.тМЛ The verse (11 + 11: 11 +
11: 8 + 8 = 60) should be called ati┼Ыakvar─л rather than vir─Бс╕Н aс╣гс╣нi.
Verses 11 and 12 are reckoned to the svastyayana gaс╣Зa (see note to
K─Бu┼Ы. 25. 36).

Griffith

O Prithivi, auspicious be thy woodlands, auspicious be thy hills and snow-clad mountains. Unslain, unwounded, unsubdued, I have set foot upon the Earth, On earth brown, black, ruddy and every-coloured, on the firm earth that Indra guards from danger.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What is thy middle, O earth, and what thy navel, what refreshments
    (┼л╠Бrj) arose (sam-bh┼л) out of thy bodyтАФin them do thou set us; be
    purifying (p┼л) toward us; earth (bh┼л╠Бmi) is mother, I am earth’s son;
    Parjanya is fatherтАФlet him save (fill? pс╣Ы) us.
Notes

Ppp. reads at end of a ya┼Ы ca n─Бdy─Б.

Griffith

O Prithivi, thy centre and thy navel, all forces that have issued from thy body Set us amid those forces; breathe upon us. I am the son of Earth, Earth is my Mother. Parjanya is my Sire; may he promote me.

Whitney
Translation
  1. On what earth (bh┼л╠Бmi) they enclose the sacrificial hearth; on what
    [earth] men of all works extend the sacrifice; on what earth are set
    up (mi) the sacrificial posts, erect, bright, before the oblationтАФlet
    that earth (bh┼л╠Бmi), increasing, make us increase.
Notes

Ppp. reads in b vi┼Ыvakarmaс╣Зaс╕е, and in d reads and combines
┼Ыukr─Б тАЭhuty─Б pur-. All the mss. accent at the end vardham─Бn─Б╠Б. In
V─Бit. 15. 8, the verse is used to accompany the enclosing of the
sacrificial hearth. In virtue of one jagat─л p─Бda (b), the verse is
a full ┼Ыakvar─л (56 syll.).

    vex [us] with mind, who with deadly weaponтАФhim, O prior-acting earth
    (bh┼л╠Бmi), do thou put in our power.

‘Prior-acting,’ i.e., apparently, ‘getting the start of him’; we should
expect a nom. rather than a vocative case. Ppp. reads instead
p┼лrvakс╣Ыtvane; also, in b, тАШbhimany─Б t─Бindanam─Б dhanena. Read in
our text pс╣Ыtany─Б╠Бd y├▓ (an accent-sign omitted); one of our mss. тМКand
five of SPP’s authorities, and his text!тМЛ, however, read y├│. According
to the usual nomenclature of the Anukr., the verse is a vir─Бс╕Н g─Бyatr─л
(11 + 11: 12 = 34, hence bhurij). тМКDr. Ryder suggests that the
mah─Бbс╣Ыhat─л here intended is one of 3 j─Бgata p─Бdas (see Ind. Stud.
viii. 243-4). Both this vs. and 17 may be scanned as 12 + 12: 12тАФcf.
under vs. 17.тМЛ

Griffith

The man who hates us, Earth! who fights against us, who threaten us with thought or deadly weapon, make him our thrall as thou hast done aforetime.

резрел рддреНрд╡рдЬреНрдЬрд╛рддрд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдпрд┐ рдЪрд░рдиреНрддрд┐ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Born from thee, mortals go about upon thee; thou bearest bipeds,
    thou quadrupeds; thine, O earth, are these five [races] of men, for
    whom, mortals, the rising sun extends with his rays immortal light.
Notes

Ppp. reads in b ca instead of the second tvam.

Griffith

Produced from thee, on thee move mortal creatures: thou bearest them, both quadruped and biped. Thine, Prithivi, are these Five human Races, for whom, though mortal, Surya as he rises spreads with his rays the light that is immortal.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Thou hast become great, a great station (sadh├бstha) great is thy
    trembling, stirring, quaking; great Indra defends thee unremittingly. Do
    thou, O earth (bh┼л╠Бmi), make us to shine forth as in the aspect
    (saс╣Бdс╣Ы╠Б┼Ы) of gold; let no one soever hate us.
Notes

Ppp. reads v─лryeс╣Зa for apram─Бdam in c, and from e
тМКsamdс╣Ы┼ЫiтМЛ passes directly on to our 19 c (agnir antaс╣г pur-
etc.): probably an accidental omission. The verse (12 + 11: 8 + 8 + 8 =
58) lacks two syllables of a full ati┼Ыakvar─л.

Griffith

A vast abode hast thou become, the Mighty. Great stress is on thee, press and agitation, but with unceasing care great Indra guards thee. So make us shine, O Earth, us with the splendour of gold. Let no man look on us with hatred.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Agni is in the earth (bh┼л╠Бmi), in the herbs; the waters bear Agni;
    Agni [is] in the stones (├б┼Ыman); Agni is within men; in kine, in
    horses are Agnis.
Notes

This and the two following verses are quite out of connection here, and
seem to be an intrusion. They are quoted together in K─Бu┼Ы. 2. 41 as
accompanying the feeding of the fire with fuel; in 120. 5, in a ceremony
against the cleaving open of the ground; and in 137. 30 (each singly) to
accompany the strewing of the sacrificial hearth in the ─Бjyatantra.
The first part of the verse (as noted above) is wanting in Ppp.

Griffith

Agni is in the earth, in plants; the waters hold Agni in them, in the stones is Agni. Agni abideth deep in men: Agnis abide in cows and steeds.

Whitney
Translation
  1. On the earth (bh┼л╠Бmi) they give to the gods the sacrifice, the
    oblation, duly prepared; on the earth (bh┼л╠Бmi) mortal men (manuс╣гy├а)
    live by svadh─Б╠Б, by food; let that earth (bh┼л╠Бmi) assign us breath,
    life-time; let earth make me one who attains old age.
Notes

The verse (8 + 8: 8 + 8: 11 + 11 = 54) should be called by the Anukr.
svar─Бj instead of vir─Бj. Ppp. reads in a juhvati instead of
dadati.

Griffith

On earth they offer sacrifice and dressed oblation to the Gods. Men, mortals, live upon the earth by food in their accustomed way. May that Earth grant us breath and vital power. Prithivi give me life of long duration!

рднреВрдореНрдпрд╛реСрдореНред рджреЗреТрд╡реЗрднреНрдпрдГреСред рджреТрджреТрддрд┐реТред рдпреТрдЬреНрдЮрдореНред рд╣реТрд╡реНрдпрдореНред рдЕрд░реСрдореНрд╜рдХреГрддрдореНред рднреВрдореНрдпрд╛реСрдореНред рдореТрдиреБреТрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГс│бред рдЬреАреТрд╡реТрдиреНрддрд┐реТред рд╕реНрд╡реТрдзрдпрд╛реСред рдЕрдиреНрдиреЗреСрдиред рдорд░реНрддреНрдпрд╛рдГреСред рд╕рд╛ред рдирдГреТред рднреВрдорд┐рдГреСред рдкреНрд░рд╛реТрдгрдореНред рдЖрдпреБрдГреСред рджреТрдзрд╛реТрддреБреТред рдЬреТрд░рддреНрд╜рдЕреСрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдореНред рдорд╛реТред рдкреГреТрдерд┐реТрд╡реАред рдХреГреТрдгреЛреТрддреБреТред рез.реиреиред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рднреВрдореНрдпрд╛рдореН) рднреВрдорд┐ рдкрд░ (рджреЗрд╡реЗрднреНрдпрдГ) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп (рд╣рд╡реНрдпрдореН) рджреЗрдиреЗ-рд▓реЗрдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп, (рдЕрд░рдВрдХреГрддрдореН) рд╢реЛрднрд┐рдд рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╡рд╛ рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐рдорд╛рдиреН рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореН) рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд┐рдХрд░рдг рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рдХреЛ (рджрджрддрд┐) рджрд╛рди рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВред (рднреВрдореНрдпрд╛рдореН) рднреВрдорд┐ рдкрд░ (рдорд░реНрддреНрдпрд╛рдГ) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп (рд╕реНрд╡рдзрдпрд╛) рдЕрдкрдиреА рдзрд╛рд░рдг рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐ рд╕реЗ (рдЕрдиреНрдиреЗрди) рдЕрдиреНрди рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ (рдЬреАрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐) рдЬреАрд╡рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВред (рд╕рд╛ рднреВрдорд┐рдГ) рд╡рд╣ рднреВрдорд┐ (рдирдГ) рд╣рдо рдХреЛ (рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдореН) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдг [рдЖрддреНрдордмрд▓] рдФрд░ (рдЖрдпреБрдГ) рдЖрдпреБ [рдЬреАрд╡рди] (рджрдзрд╛рддреБ) рджреЗрд╡реЗ, рдФрд░ [рд╡рд╣реА] (рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА) рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА (рдорд╛) рдореБрдЭ рдХреЛ (рдЬрд░рджрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдореН) рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛ рднреЛрдЬрдирд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рдХреГрдгреЛрддреБ) рдХрд░реЗ реереиреирее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Whitney
Translation
  1. What odor of thine, O earth, came into being, which the herbs,
    which the waters bear, which the Gandharvas and Apsarases sharedтАФwith
    that do thou make me odorous; let no one soever hate us.

the latter’s system admits. Verses 23-25 тМКso the schol.тМЛ are called in
K─Бu┼Ы. 13. 12 and 54. 5 gandhaprav─Бd─Бs (likewise in the comm. to 24.

Griffith

Scent that hath risen from thee, O Earth, the fragrance which. growing herbs and plants and waters carry, Shared by Apsarases, shared by Gandharvas therewith make thou me sweet: let no man hate me.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Rock [is?] earth (bh┼л╠Бmi), stone, dust; this earth (bh┼л╠Бmi)
    [is] held together, held; to that earth, gold-backed (-v├бkс╣гas) have
    I paid homage.
Notes

Ppp. reads, in a-b, p─Бс╣Еsv ary─Б bh┼лmi stс╣Ыt─Б dhс╣Ыt─Б, and omits c,
d. тМКCf. note to vs. 6.тМЛ

Griffith

Rock earth, and stone, and dust, this Earth is held together,. firmly bound. To this gold-breasted Prithivi mine adoration have I paid.

  1. On whom stand always fixed the trees, the forest trees

Whitney
Translation
  1. Arising (ud-─лr), also sitting, standing, striding forth, with
    right and left feet, let us not stagger upon the earth.
Notes

The Anukr. seems to assume the resolution -kс╣Ы-─Б- in b. This verse
and 33 below are quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 24. 33 to accompany the taking of three
steps, while looking around, in the ─Бgrah─Бyaс╣З─л ceremony.

Griffith

Sitting at ease or rising up, standing or going on our way. With our right foot and with our left we will not reel upon the earth.

  1. Let cleansed (┼Ыuddh├б) waters flow for our body; what mucus (?

Translation
  1. What forward directions are thine, what upward, what are thine, O
    earth (bh┼л╠Бmi), downward, and what behind, let those be pleasant to me
    going about; let me not fall down [when] supported (┼Ыri) on creation
    (bh├║vana).
Notes

The verse is found also in MS. (iv. 14. 11), which reads, for b,
y─Б╠Б┼Ы ca bh┼лmy adhar─Б╠Бg y─Б╠Б┼Ы ca pa┼Ыc─Б╠Б; also ┼Ыiv─Б╠Бs for syon─Б╠Бs in c.
Ppp. has in b bh─Бume тАШdhar─Бd, and in d ┼Ыu┼Ыriy─Бс╣Зe. This and
the following verse are reckoned to the svastyayana gaс╣Зa: see note to
K─Бu┼Ы. 25. 36.

Griffith

Earth, be thine eastern and thy northern regions, those lying southward and those lying westward. Propitious unto me in all my movements. Long as I tread the ground let me not stumble.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Do not push (nud) us behind, nor in front, nor above and below;
    become thou welfare for us, O earth (bh┼л╠Бmi); let not the waylayers
    find [us]; keep very far off the deadly weapon.
Notes

The directions ‘forward’ etc., in this and the preceding verse, are also
equivalent, as elsewhere, to ’eastern’ etc. P─Бda d occurs below as
xiv. 2. 11 a; e was found above as i. 20. 3 d etc. Ppp.
reads m─Б for nas in a, omits b, reads in c bh─Бume me
kс╣Ыс╣Зu, and makes d and e change places, reading also v─Бyas for
var─лyas тМКand vidhan for vidanтМЛ. The verse (11 + 8: 8 + 8 + 8 = 43)
is curiously defined by the Anukr.

Griffith

Drive us not from the west or east, drive us not from the north or south, Be gracious unto us, O Earth: let not the robbers find us; keep the deadly weapon far away.

    for ally (med├нn), so far let my sight not fail (m─л), from one year

Griffith

Long as, on thee, I look around, possessing Surya as a friend, So long, through each succeeding year, let not my power of vision fail.

Whitney
Translation
  1. In that, lying, I turn myself about upon the right [or] the left
    side, O earth (bh┼л╠Бmi); in that we with our ribs lie stretched out upon
    thee that meetest usтАФdo not in that case injure us, O earth (bh┼л╠Бmi),
    thou underlier of everything.
Notes

‘Underlier,’ lit. ‘counter-lier, one whose lying answers to that of
another.’ In a, b, perhaps rather ‘in that I turn over toward
[thee] the one or the other side’ тМКcf. vii. 100. 1тМЛ. Our Bp. puts its
sign of p─Бda-division between c and d before instead of after
y├бt, and the Anukr. supports it by counting a bс╣Ыhat─л element in the
verse (which is properly 8 + 11: 8 + 8: 8 + 8 = 51). The verse is
prescribed in Kaug. 24. 30, to accompany the act of turning over while
lying down, in the ─Бgrah─Бyaс╣З─л ceremony. All the mss., with the
edition, тМКlikewise SPP’s mss. and ed.,тМЛ accent pary─Б┬┤varte; it should
ht pary─Бv├бrte. Ppp. puts the verse after 35, and reads api for
abhi in b; and, for d, pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нv─Б yad с╣Ыdva ┼Ыemahe; and bh─Бume
both times for bh┼лme.

Griffith

When, as I lie, O Earth, I turn upon my right side and my left, When stretched at all our length we lay our ribs on thee who meetest us. Do us no injury there, O Earth who furnishest a bed for all.

рейрел рдпрддреНрддреЗ рднреВрдореЗ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. What of thee, O earth (bh┼л╠Бmi), I dig out, let that quickly grow
    over; let me not hit (arpay-) thy vitals nor thy heart, O cleansing
    one.
Notes

‘Grow over,’ i.e. heal up, like a wound. Ppp. has again bh─Бume in
a; also oс╣гaс╣Б for kс╣гipram in b, and arpitam in d; this
time (cf. vs. 29) it agrees with our text in the peculiar epithet
vimс╣Ыgvari, lit. ‘wiping off.’ K─Бu┼Ы. (46. 51) quotes the verse to
accompany an act of digging in a pr─Бya┼Ыcitta ceremony; and again
similarly at 137. 12.

Griffith

Let what I dig from thee, O Earth, rapidly spring and grow again. O Purifier, let me not pierce through thy vitals or thy heart.

Griffith

Earth, may thy summer, and thy rains, and autumn, thy winter, and thy dewy frosts, and spring-time. May thy years, Prithivi! and ordered seasons, and day and night pour out for us abundance.

Whitney
Translation
  1. She who, cleansing one, trembling away the serpent; on whom were the
    fires that are within the waters, abandoning the god-insulting
    barbarians, choosing, she the earth, Indra [and] not Vс╣Ыitra, kept
    herself (dhс╣Ы) for the mighty one (┼Ыakr├б), the virile bull.
Notes

The first p─Бda is extremely obscure; it is here translated mechanically,
as closely as possible to the text. Bruce understands at the beginning
y─Б╠Б: ─Б╠Бpa (instead of the y─Б╠Б: ├бpa of the pada-text); and that would
be a natural and easy emendation, if only the resulting sense were more
acceptable. Ludwig renders as if we read s├бrp─Бt (’trembling at the
serpent’). The totally different reading of Ppp., ya ─Бpas sarpan
yatam─Бn─Б vimс╣Ыgvari, indicates that the text is corrupt. Ppp. further
reads in b agnayo тАШpsv, and stops the verse at dadat─л, then
adding our vs. 40. Our verse (12 + 11: 11 + 11: 11 = 56) adds up as a
true ┼Ыakvar─л.

Griffith

The purifier, shrinking from the Serpent, she who held fires that lie within the waters, Who gives as prey the God-blaspheming Dasyus, Earth choosing Indra for her Lord, not Vritra, hath clung to Sakra, to the Strong and Mighty.

Whitney
Translation
  1. On whom are the seat and oblation-holder; on whom the sacrificial
    post (y┼л╠Бpa) is planted; on whom worshipers (brahm├бn) praise (arc)
    with verses, with the chant, knowing the sacrificial formulas; on whom
    are joined the priests (с╣Ыtv├нj), for Indra to drink the soma;тАФ
Notes

Ppp. reads in e yujyante тАШsy─Бm с╣Ыtyavas s-. The verse is quoted in
K─Бu┼Ы. 24. 37 to accompany an oblation тМКand by D─Бrila to 24. 24, in the
─Бgrah─Бyaс╣З─л ceremonyтМЛ. It is also reckoned with vs. 1 among the
puс╣гс╣нika mantras (see note to K─Бu┼Ы. 19. i). In V─Бit. 15. 4, this verse
and the two following are prescribed to accompany the subrahmaс╣Зy─Б
recitation; in 10. 8, it is used at the setting up of the sacrificial
post.

Griffith

Base of the seat and sheds, on whom the sacrificial stake is reared, On whom the Yajus-knowing priests recite their hymns and chant their psalms, And ministers are busied that Indra may drink the Soma juice;

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдореН) рдЬрд┐рд╕ [рднреВрдорд┐] рдкрд░ (рд╕рджреЛрд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрдзрд╛рдиреЗ) рд╕рднрд╛ рдФрд░ рдЕрдиреНрдирд╕реНрдерд╛рди рд╣реИрдВ, (рдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдореН) рдЬрд┐рд╕ рдкрд░ (рдпреВрдкрдГ) рдЬрдпрд╕реНрддрдореНрдн (рдирд┐рдореАрдпрддреЗ) рдЧрд╛рдбрд╝рд╛ рдЬрд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИред (рдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдореН) рдЬрд┐рд╕ рдкрд░ (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рдгрдГ) рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛ [рд╡реЗрджрд╡реЗрддреНрддрд╛] рд▓реЛрдЧ (рдЛрдЧреНрднрд┐рдГ) рдЛрдЪрд╛рдУрдВ [рд╡реЗрджрд╡рд╛рдгрд┐рдпреЛрдВ] рд╕реЗ рдФрд░ (рдпрдЬреБрд░реНрд╡реЗрджрдГ) рдпрдЬреБрд░реНрд╡реЗрджреА [рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рджреЗрд╡ рдХреА рдкреВрдЬрд╛ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ] рд▓реЛрдЧ (рд╕рд╛рдореНрдирд╛) рдореЛрдХреНрд╖рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде [рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЛ] (рдЕрд░реНрдЪрдиреНрддрд┐) рдкреВрдЬрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВред (рдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдореН) рдЬрд┐рд╕ рдкрд░ (рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрдГ) рд╕рдм рдЛрддреБрдУрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮ [рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХрд╛ рдкреВрдЬрди] рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ [рдпреЛрдЧреА рдЬрди] (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдп) рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ [рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрдд рдЬреАрд╡] рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рд╕реЛрдордореН) рд╕реЛрдо [рдЕрдореГрдд, рдореЛрдХреНрд╖рд╕реБрдЦ] (рдкрд╛рддрд╡реЗ) рдкрд╛рди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдХреЛ (рдпреБрдЮреНрдЬрдиреНрддреЗ) рд╕рдорд╛рдзрд┐ рд▓рдЧрд╛рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ реерейреорее

    Bhaga join on after; let Indra go [as our] forerunner.

given here s─Б naс╣г pa┼Ы┼лn vi┼Ыvar┼лp─Бn dadh─Бtu jaradaс╣гс╣нiс╣Б m─Б pс╣Ыthiv─л

May she, the Earth, assign to us the opulence for which we yearn, May Bhaga share and aid the task and Indra come to lead the way.

Translation
  1. On whom, the earth (bh┼л╠Бmi), mortals sing [and] dance with loud
    noises (? vy─Б├мlaba); on whom they fight; on whom speaks the shout
    (─Бkrand├б), the drumтАФlet that earth (bh┼л╠Бmi) push forth our rivals;
    let earth make me free from rivals.

11 + 11 = 54) has no kakubh element in it, but as ┼Ыakvar─л it is
vir─Бj. Ppp. puts the verse after our vs. 42, and reads for b:
jan─Б marty─Б dv─Бilav─Б; тМКin c yudhyante тАШsy─Бm; and, for e, f,
s─Б no bh┼лmiс╣г pra dadhat─Бс╣Б sapatn─Бс╣Е: yo no dveс╣гс╣нy adharaс╣Б taс╣Б kс╣Ыс╣Зotu.

Griffith

May she, the Earth, whereon men sing and dance with varied shout and noise, Whereon men meet in battle, and the war-cry and the drum resound, May she drive off our foemen, may Prithivi rid me of my foes.

May Earth the Goddess, she who bears her treasure stored up in many a place, gold, gems, and riches, Giver of opulence, grant great possessions to us bestowing them with love and favour.

рекрел рдЬрдирдВ рдмрд┐рднреНрд░рддреА ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Let the earth, bearing in many places people of different speech, of
    diverse customs (-dh├бrman), according to their homes, yield (duh) me
    a thousand streams of property, like a steady (dhruv├б) unresisting
    milch-cow.
Notes

Ppp. reads in a janaс╣Б yaс╣Б bibhrat─л bahuv─Бcasaс╣Б, and in c nas
for me. The Anukr. does not heed that the last p─Бda in this verse, and
the last two in vs. 44, are triс╣гс╣нubh. тМКKe┼Ы., p. 322┬│┬╣, couples this vs.
with the preceding: cf. note to vs. 44.тМЛ

Griffith

Earth, bearing folk of many a varied language with divers rites as suits their dwelling-places, Pour, like a constant cow that never faileth, a thousand streams of treasure to enrich me!

Whitney
Translation
  1. What stinging (vс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыcika) harsh-biting serpent of thine lies in
    secret, winter-harmed, torpid (? bhс╣Ыmal├б); whatever worm, O earth,
    becoming lively, stirs in the early rainy seasonтАФlet that, crawling, not
    crawl upon us; be thou gracious to us with that which is propitious.
Notes

Ppp. reads in a vс╣Ы┼Ыcakas, and for b ff. hemantalabdho
bhramalo (!) kс╣Ыmir lisaс╣Б pс╣Ыthivy─Бi pr─Бvс╣Ыс╣г─л yad ejati. The treatment of
kr├нmis in c as neuter is very strange. тМКIs it a collective neuter
like Gew├╝rm? cf. Noun-Inflection, JAOS. x. 570.тМЛ In the description
of the verse (11 + 12: 7 + 8 + 8 + 8 = 54) by the Anukr. there is
perhaps something omitted (or we are to read vir─Бс╣н ┼Ыakvar─л for
par─Б┼Ы-). The verse is used according to K─Бu┼Ы. 50. 17 (with тМКiii. 26
(see introduction thereto) and 27 andтМЛ vi. 56. 1) in the removal of
vermin; also, according to 139. 8, with a number of other verses about
serpents and the like; and it is reckoned to the r─Бudra gaс╣Зa (note to
K─Бu┼Ы. 50. 13). In V─Бit. 29. 10 it accompanies a libation to Rudra.

Griffith

Thy snake, thy sharply stinging scorpion, lying concealed, be- wildered, chilled with cold of winter, The worm, O Prithivi, each thing that in the Rains revives and stirs, Creeping, forbear to creep on us! With all things gracious bless thou us.

рекрен рдпреЗ рддреЗ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. What many roads thou hast, for people to go upon, a track
    (v├бrtman) for the chariot, and for the going of the cart, by which
    (pl.) men of both kinds, excellent and evil, go aboutтАФthat road, free
    from enemies, free from robbers, may we conquer; be thou gracious to us
    with that which is propitious.
Notes

Ppp. reads bahudh─Б (for bahavas) in a, yebhi┼Ы car- at
beginning of c, and panth─Бm in d; and it omits the last p─Бda
тМКrepeated from vs. 46тМЛ. The prat─лka (ye te panth─Бnaс╕е), quoted in
K─Бu┼Ы. 50. 1, might refer either to this verse or to vii. 55. 1; the
comm. to vii. 55 declares the latter to be intended.

Griffith

Thy many ways on which the people travel, the road for car and wain to journey over, Thereon meet both the good and bad, that pathway may we attain without a foe or robber. With all things gracious bless thou us.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Bearing the fool, bearer of what is heavy, enduring (titikс╣г├║) the
    death (? nidh├бna) of the excellent and of the evil, the earth, in
    concord with the boar, opens itself to the wild (mс╣Ыg├б) hog.
Notes

Ludwig understands gurubhс╣Ы╠Бt in a as ‘bearer of the wise’ (guru
as antithesis of malva); the Pet. Lexx. translate nidh├бna as
‘residence’ (and so Bruce, ‘abode’). Ppp. has at the beginning a very
different text: sarpaс╣Б bibhrat─л surabhir; and it reads s┼лkareс╣Зa in
c and var─Бh─Бya in d.

Griffith

Supporting both the foolish and the weighty she bears the death both of the good and evil. In friendly concord with the boar, Earth opens herself for the wild swine that roams the forest.

    here.

Griffith

All sylvan beasts of thine that love the woodlands, man-eaters,. forest-haunting, lions, tigers, Hyena, wolf, Misfortune, evil spirit, drive from us, chase the demons to a distance.

Translation
  1. She to whom two-footed winged-ones fly together, swans, eagles,
    hawks, birds; on whom the wind, M─Бtari┼Ыvan, goes about, making clouds of
    dust (? r├бjas) and setting in motion the treesтАФflame (arc├нs) blows
    after the forth-blowing, the toward-blowing, of the wind.
Notes

The second p─Бda is identical with xi. 2. 24 b. Upav─Б╠Бm is
metrically an intrusion into e: with the p─Бda is to be compared RV.
i. 148. 4 c (which, however, casts little light upon it). Ppp. reads
in c-d v─Бtayate m─Бtari┼Ыv─Б raj-; and, in e, it omits upav─Бm,
and has at the end arciс╣гe. The Anukr. appears to divide the last
redundant p─Бda into two, an anuс╣гс╣нubh (8) and a kakubh (6); the whole
makes two syllables more than a proper ┼Ыakvar─л (11 + 11: 11 + 11: 8 +
6 = 58). тМКHopkins, JAOS. xx.┬▓ 217, thinks that fire caused by the
friction of branches is here alluded to, and cites parallels. We may add
Indische Spr├╝che, 3759, which is very clear.тМЛ

Griffith

To whom the winged bipeds fly together, birds of each various kind, the swans, the eagles; On whom the Wind comes rushing, Matarisvan, rousing the dust and causing trees to tremble, and flame pursues the blast. hither and thither;

    [are] disposed upon the earth (bh┼л╠Бmi); the broad (pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Б) earth

Griffith

Earth, upon whom are settled, joined together, the night and day, the dusky and the ruddy, Prithivi compassed by the rain about her, Happily may she stablish us in each delightful dwelling place.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Both heaven and earth and atmosphere [have given] me this expanse;
    fire, sun, waters, and all the gods have together given me wisdom
    (medh─Б╠Б).
Notes

The translation of a, b is doubtful; vy├бcas may be in apposition
with ant├бrikс╣гam, and the gift as in the second line. The Anukr. takes
no notice of the irregular combination me тАЩdam in a, which is
needed to make the verse a simple anuс╣гс╣нubh. Ppp. combines m─Бi тАЩdaс╣Б,
and it has at the end saс╣Б dadh─Бu. Not this verse, but vi. 53. 1
(according to the comm. on the latter), is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 10. 20, in a
ceremony for wisdom; тМКbut D─Бrila understands our verse as the one
intendedтМЛ.

Griffith

Heaven, Earth, the realm of Middle Air have granted me this ample room, Agni, Sun, Waters, all the Gods have joined to give me mental power.

Griffith

There, when the Gods, O Goddess, named thee, spreading thy wide expanse as thou wast broadening eastward, Then into thee passed many a charm and glory: thou madest for thyself the world’s four regions.

Translation

    upon the earth since (y─Б╠Бt) she was bornтАФpleasing, going at the head,

Translation
  1. What I speak, rich in honey I speak it; what I view, that they win
    (? van) me; brilliant am I, possessed of swiftness; I smite down others
    that are violent (? d├│dhat).
Notes

The sense of b is obscure. Ppp. reads vadantu (for vananti); Bp.
has vadanti, and O.s.m. (p.m.?) vahanti. Ppp. has at the end
dodhata. K─Бu┼Ы. quotes the verse at 24. 14 and 38. 29, each time adding
mantroktam ‘as expressed in the verse.’ тМКPpp. puts this verse before
our 57.тМЛ

Griffith

Whate’er I say I speak with honey-sweetness, whatever I behold for that they love me. Dazzling, impetuous am I: others who fiercely stir I slay.

ремрез рддреНрд╡рдорд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╡рдкрдиреА рдЬрдирд╛рдирд╛рдорджрд┐рддрд┐рдГ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Thou art the scatterer (? ─Бv├бpana) of people, [art] a
    wish-fulfilling (k─Бmad├║gha) Aditi, spreading out; what of thee is
    deficient, may Praj─Бpati, first-born of righteousness, fill that up for
    thee.
Notes

The word ─Бv├бpana seems to mean sometimes, and perhaps here, a (wide,
shallow?) receptacle onto which things are strewn or scattered. Ppp. has
at the beginning vim for tvam, and in b vi┼Ыvar┼лp─Б for
paprath─Бn─Б; for c, d it reads yat t─Бu тАЭnaс╣Б tat t─Бp┼лray─Бti
praj─Бpatiс╕е praj─Бbhis saс╣Бvid─Бn─Бm; and it ends the hymn here. The Anukr.
refuses to admit two familiar resolutions in a, and gratuitously
calls the p─Бda a b─Бrhata (9 syll.). The second half-verse is twice
quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. (46. 52; 137. 13) in connection with filling up a hole
that has been dug (iti saс╣Бvapati) and the verse, in 137. 14, with
removing elsewhither the dirt taken out.

Griffith

Thou art the vessel that containeth people, Aditi, granter of the wish, far-spreading. Prajapati, the first-born Son of Order, supplieth thee with what- soe’er thou lackest.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let slanders upon thee, free from disease, free from y├бkс╣гma, be
    produced (pr├бs┼лta) for us, O earth; awakening to meet our long
    lifetime, may we be tribute-bearers to thee.
Notes

The sense of upasth─Б╠Бs (p. upaре░sth─Б╠Бс╕е) in a is doubtful; Ludwig
renders ’laps,’ as if up├бsth─Бs; тМКand so BloomfieldтМЛ; Bruce ’that shall
dwell in thee.’ The verse is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 50. 10, in a ceremony for
success. The description of the Anukr. is unintelligible, as the verse
is a perfectly regular triс╣гс╣нubh.

Griffith

Let thy breasts, frec from sickness and Consumption, be. Prithivi, produced for our advantage. Through long-extended life wakeful and watching still may we be thy tributary servants.

Whitney
Translation
  1. O mother earth (bh┼л╠Бmi), do thou kindly set me down well
    established; in concord with the heaven, O sage (k├бvi), do thou set me
    in fortune, in prosperity (bh┼л╠Бti).
Notes

The verse is used by K─Бu┼Ы. (24. 27) in connection with vss. 1-7; also by
the comm. to 58. 19 in the annapr─Б┼Ыana ceremony. V─Бit. 27. 8
prescribes it on descending from the sacrificial post (cf. note to vs.
33). тМКFor ┼Ыriy─Б╠Бm, the only form of its kind in the AV., see JAOS. x.
389.тМЛ

тМКHere ends the first anuv─Бka, of 1 hymn and 63 verses. The quoted
Anukr. says bh─Бumas tryadhik─Б с╣гaс╣гс╣нiс╕е.

Griffith

O Earth, my Mother, set thou me happily in a place secure. Of one accord with Heaven, O Sage, set me in glory and in wealth.
